<div id="review_1655502718" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1655502718" />
    <a title="Kimberly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17371689-kimberly"><img alt="Kimberly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1404147069p2/17371689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1655502718?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kimberly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kimberly" href="/user/show/17371689-kimberly">Kimberly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17371689-kimberly?shelf=story-collections">story-collections</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1655502718&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1655502718" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8240780696354891695">THE KING IN YELLOW and OTHER HORROR STORIES is a collection of stories based upon the book "The King in Yellow", and then some stories at the end that--quite frankly--didn't seem to have anything in common with the earlier ones. I have to admit that the horror stories were my absolute favorites--to the extant that even though I didn't care at all for some of the later ones, I'm still giving this collection a solid four stars based on the strength of the tales I DID like.<br/><br/>The "horror" tales are ar</span>
  <span id="freeText8240780696354891695" style="display:none">THE KING IN YELLOW and OTHER HORROR STORIES is a collection of stories based upon the book "The King in Yellow", and then some stories at the end that--quite frankly--didn't seem to have anything in common with the earlier ones. I have to admit that the horror stories were my absolute favorites--to the extant that even though I didn't care at all for some of the later ones, I'm still giving this collection a solid four stars based on the strength of the tales I DID like.<br /><br />The "horror" tales are are loosely woven around the idea that anyone reading the book, "The King in Yellow", is led to madness or some horrific event. The really beauty of this, in my opinion, is that the references to the book itself are so obscure, that the reader really doesn't know exactly what the book is about! This just added to the mystery and atmosphere of psychological horror, leaving you to ponder what exactly these people are reading.......<br /><br />As I stated earlier, there were some stories in here that I really didn't like much at all, but this collection was worthwhile solely for the ones focusing on the King. Those stories are ones that I will definitely be re-reading in the future.<br /><br />Recommended!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8240780696354891695" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText10967237256847403371" style="display:none"><i>The King in Yellow</i> is a medieval play infamous for inducing madness and despair among its readers, a monstrosity denunciated by pulpit and press, the one its author shot himself for bringing forth.<br />It is fictional.<br /><br />This book contains concatenated weird macabre(and amazing) short stories, built around the above-mentioned infamous and forbidden play.<br />They are fictional too.<br /><br />It would be probably safe to tag above collection as proto-lovecraftian since passing references to the <i>Yellow King</i>, <i>Hastur</i> and <i>Lake of Hali</i> often find their place in <i>Cthulhu</i> mythos, and further 'fear of the unknown' stories it inspired (including <i>True Detective</i>).<br />Fictional again.<br /><br />Book in a book in a book.<br /><b>Bookception :)</b></span>

<div id="review_1196701939" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1196701939" />
    <a title="Kyell Gold" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8811583-kyell-gold"><img alt="Kyell Gold" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442476155p2/8811583.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1196701939?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kyell Gold" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kyell Gold" href="/user/show/8811583-kyell-gold">Kyell Gold</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1196701939" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9760839969392540771">I've heard about this book for twenty-some years now, ever since reading James Blish's short story "More Light" (in the out of print collection "Alchemy and Academe"). Finally I got my hands on it and had a chance to read through the origin of the "King in Yellow" mythos.<br/><br/>The introduction to this volume, by E.F. Bleiler, is worth reading, as it sets the expectations well for what you're about to read. Bleiler is no fan of most of Chambers' work and makes no secret of it (I was surprised to learn </span>
  <span id="freeText9760839969392540771" style="display:none">I've heard about this book for twenty-some years now, ever since reading James Blish's short story "More Light" (in the out of print collection "Alchemy and Academe"). Finally I got my hands on it and had a chance to read through the origin of the "King in Yellow" mythos.<br /><br />The introduction to this volume, by E.F. Bleiler, is worth reading, as it sets the expectations well for what you're about to read. Bleiler is no fan of most of Chambers' work and makes no secret of it (I was surprised to learn that Chambers was a very popular novelist in his day), but he has chosen the stories that he feels are a cut above the rest, that are worth reading and preserving. I also referred back to the intro when reading some of the later stories for reasons I will mention again below.<br /><br />One of the expectations I had when starting this book was that I would find stories similar to H.P. Lovecraft's; Chambers is cited as an influence on Lovecraft, and they'd become linked in my mind because of the similar notions of hapless humans living in a world ruled by horrible great powers. The book starts very strongly with the story "The Yellow Sign," probably the closest story to fulfilling that expectation in the whole volume. As you move along through time with the stories, the horror element diminishes. Often you will read characters exclaiming on the horror and the terror of something they've seen--a familiar device to anyone who knows Lovecraft's work, but Chambers is usually unable to follow through as Lovecraft was. The reveals fall flat and at the end of many stories, I was left unsatisfied--not only for the lack of a Lovecraftian italicized horrific reveal, but also because Chambers' story construction is often weak, leaving me wondering what the point of the story was at all.<br /><br />Returning to the intro, I saw Bleiler's note that he included some of the stories not because of their overall quality necessarily, but because they held some strongly-written scenes that he quite liked. He emphasized Chambers' skill with description, and when I went back and read the stories in this light, I appreciated them much more. The two strong points of this collection are the human relationships and the descriptions. "On the silver shoal the waves washed and washed, breaking like crushed opals where the sands sang with the humming froth." That's from a random page I opened to in the collection. This kind of stuff is all through his stories, and if you grow impatient with the stories themselves, just stop and marvel at the words. <br /><br />The last three stories are taken from a chaptered novel about a biologist encountering strange and wonderful and sometimes extinct creatures, and are meant to be more humorous than horrible. His narrator in these stories is a very strong character and when I stopped expecting horror from his stories, I enjoyed them quite a bit.<br /><br />There's a lot to like here, and I think the key to appreciating it is to let go of any expectations you have upon picking up the book. Chambers is very good at some things and not so good at others, and if you can appreciate the good and chuckle away the bad, you will enjoy this collection quite a bit.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9760839969392540771" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_218399321" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/218399321" />
    <a title="Sesana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5172893-sesana"><img alt="Sesana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413088169p2/5172893.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/218399321?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sesana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sesana" href="/user/show/5172893-sesana">Sesana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer218399321" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16870698683947521652">A classic of weird horror, The King in Yellow is a collection of short stories. Well, the first four stories are weird horror classics. Related only by the existence and influence of the play The King in Yellow, the second act of which will inevitably drive mad any who read it, they're a set of nicely atmospheric set. What will really linger in your mind is the concept of the play, which we never get more than brief glimpses of. I'd say this is probably what makes the reputation of the book.<br/><br/>Thes</span>
  <span id="freeText16870698683947521652" style="display:none">A classic of weird horror, The King in Yellow is a collection of short stories. Well, the first four stories are weird horror classics. Related only by the existence and influence of the play The King in Yellow, the second act of which will inevitably drive mad any who read it, they're a set of nicely atmospheric set. What will really linger in your mind is the concept of the play, which we never get more than brief glimpses of. I'd say this is probably what makes the reputation of the book.<br /><br />These are followed by a wistful, traditional ghost (or, perhaps, time travel) story, and an odd bit of prose that might be an allegory that only the author had a key to, or fragments of a larger work, or a bit of inspired nonsense, but is absorbing nevertheless. <br /><br />The last four stories are completely and entirely different. Instead of horror, they're a fairly realistic look at the lives of American art students in late 19th century Paris's Latin Quarter. One of the stories is set during the 1870 siege of Paris, but there's no action aside from that. And honestly? They're right up my alley. If I had known these stories were in here, I would have been even more eager to read the book as a whole. But if you aren't interested in the lives of 19th century Parisian students? You might want to stop after The Prophet's Paradise.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16870698683947521652" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer6731264882922668066">The first four short stories? Fantastic. The third one of four - 'In the Court of the Dragon' - was probably my favorite piece of late-19th century horror fiction, well served and set up by the two stories that came before. <br/><br/>After the four short stories came some very quick ... vignettes? Ultra-short stories? Only a few lines each, but effective and interesting. An example:<br/><br/><b>THE GREEN ROOM</b><br/><br/>The Clown turned his powdered face to the mirror.<br/>"If to be fair is to be beautiful," he said, "who can compare </span>
  <span id="freeText6731264882922668066" style="display:none">The first four short stories? Fantastic. The third one of four - 'In the Court of the Dragon' - was probably my favorite piece of late-19th century horror fiction, well served and set up by the two stories that came before. <br /><br />After the four short stories came some very quick ... vignettes? Ultra-short stories? Only a few lines each, but effective and interesting. An example:<br /><br /><b>THE GREEN ROOM</b><br /><br />The Clown turned his powdered face to the mirror.<br />"If to be fair is to be beautiful," he said, "who can compare with me in my white mask?"<br />"Who can compare with him in his white mask?" I asked of Death beside me.<br />"Who can compare with me?" said Death, "for I am paler still."<br />"You are very beautiful," sighed the Clown, turning his powdered face from the mirror.<br /><br />After these shorts are a series of stories that I found so dreadfully boring that I skipped the last quarter of the book ... and still I'm more than happy to give it four stars. It came from Project Gutenberg, it's free, and it has some amazing stuff at the beginning, so I can't fault it.</span>

<div id="review_11948853" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/11948853" />
    <a title="Denise" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/732847-denise"><img alt="Denise" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1199318917p2/732847.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/11948853?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Denise" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Denise" href="/user/show/732847-denise">Denise</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">lovers of psychological horror; students of the genre</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/732847-denise?shelf=reread">reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/732847-denise?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/732847-denise?shelf=project-gutenberg">project-gutenberg</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer11948853" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11233216228772870050">(Read via <a href='http://www.gutenberg.org/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Project Gutenberg</a>, not this edition.)<br/><br/>Chambers, along with Lovecraft, is one of the grandpappies of the contemporary horror genre, and these are his masterwork: a series of connected short stories and novellas about a mysterious play (also called <i>The King In Yellow</i>) that drives a reader mad. The play itself is never more than vaguely described; the stories are about the effects it has on the minds of those who read it, and their subsequent actions. <br/><br/>This is precisely the type of horror I</span>
  <span id="freeText11233216228772870050" style="display:none">(Read via <a href="http://www.gutenberg.org/" rel="nofollow noopener">Project Gutenberg</a>, not this edition.)<br /><br />Chambers, along with Lovecraft, is one of the grandpappies of the contemporary horror genre, and these are his masterwork: a series of connected short stories and novellas about a mysterious play (also called <i>The King In Yellow</i>) that drives a reader mad. The play itself is never more than vaguely described; the stories are about the effects it has on the minds of those who read it, and their subsequent actions. <br /><br />This is precisely the type of horror I love -- there's no lovingly-described Big Scary Monster, and the horror comes from the slowly-dawning realization that one's own mind and perceptions can't be trusted anymore. Though the language takes a bit of time to truly immerse oneself into, it's still fabulous, both on the readerly level and on the meta-level of observing and analyzing just how Chambers managed to pull it off. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11233216228772870050" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/866721758?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steve" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steve" href="/user/show/739853-steve">Steve</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer866721758" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer904263369926413418">What a disappointing book. The first four or five stories in the book are very effective horror stories that sort or revolve around a play called "The King in Yellow." To read this, in several of the stories, drives the reader mad. Those stores kind of relate to one another, in tone and in the way the horror works out, and I thought I was in for a real treat. But the stories that comprise the second half of the book don't relate to or mention the King in Yellow or the yellow sign, and are instea</span>
  <span id="freeText904263369926413418" style="display:none">What a disappointing book. The first four or five stories in the book are very effective horror stories that sort or revolve around a play called "The King in Yellow." To read this, in several of the stories, drives the reader mad. Those stores kind of relate to one another, in tone and in the way the horror works out, and I thought I was in for a real treat. But the stories that comprise the second half of the book don't relate to or mention the King in Yellow or the yellow sign, and are instead kind of late Victorian romance about Bohemians in Paris.. The stories don't go anywhere and don't have any effect on you except in contrast to the great stories that begin the book.<br /><br />So I highly recommend the first four or five stories; I really enjoyed them. Then when you notice that you're not interested anymore, the good stuff is past, and just put the book down. I stayed with it, alas.</span>
  <a data-text-id="904263369926413418" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/284420008?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer284420008" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9102155436243772975">One of the first things I did with my ereader was to download free, public domain works. _The King in Yellow_ was one of them.<br/><br/>This is a curious collection of stories. In the universe of these stories, there is a two act play, titled _The King in Yellow_ which has been denounced and even banned for its deleterious effect on those who read it. Sometimes a few lines of the play are given. The play is a curious mixture of science fiction and the 19th century Decadent movement. <br/><br/>So in one story, one c</span>
  <span id="freeText9102155436243772975" style="display:none">One of the first things I did with my ereader was to download free, public domain works. _The King in Yellow_ was one of them.<br /><br />This is a curious collection of stories. In the universe of these stories, there is a two act play, titled _The King in Yellow_ which has been denounced and even banned for its deleterious effect on those who read it. Sometimes a few lines of the play are given. The play is a curious mixture of science fiction and the 19th century Decadent movement. <br /><br />So in one story, one character, after reading the play, embarks on an insane, criminal plot. In another story, a female character, after reading the play, accidentally falls into a fluid which turns things into marble. After she turns into a marble statue, her lover, in despair, kills himself. <br /><br />These stories, with its tropes of the Imaginary Book and The Object Which Causes Madness, has had an influence on horror and fantasy. The frustrating thing is that these stories could have been upped a level. The plot mechanics and prose could be improved. Though concerning the prose, it does have its moments. "Have you seen the Yellow Sign?" </span>
  <a data-text-id="9102155436243772975" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2238571838" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2238571838" />
    <a title="XPHAIEA." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33757645-xphaiea"><img alt="XPHAIEA." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593620902p2/33757645.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2238571838?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="XPHAIEA." class="user" itemprop="url" name="XPHAIEA." href="/user/show/33757645-xphaiea">XPHAIEA.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780486225005" href="/book/show/970031.The_King_in_Yellow_and_Other_Horror_Stories">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33757645-xphaiea?shelf=supernatural">supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33757645-xphaiea?shelf=american">american</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33757645-xphaiea?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33757645-xphaiea?shelf=weird-lit">weird-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33757645-xphaiea?shelf=1890s">1890s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2238571838" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16993925980936124210">This is a strange little volume. The first half contains four short stories centering around the fictional story of The King in Yellow, which sends anyone who reads it utterly mad. These are striking and original horror stories with a penchant for detail and the grotesque. A man who is reclusive and works as a 'restorer of reputations' keeps a cat who mauls him ferociously and rolls around on the floor his legs curled up towards the ceiling like a dead spider. A newly built park contains a chamb</span>
  <span id="freeText16993925980936124210" style="display:none">This is a strange little volume. The first half contains four short stories centering around the fictional story of The King in Yellow, which sends anyone who reads it utterly mad. These are striking and original horror stories with a penchant for detail and the grotesque. A man who is reclusive and works as a 'restorer of reputations' keeps a cat who mauls him ferociously and rolls around on the floor his legs curled up towards the ceiling like a dead spider. A newly built park contains a chamber in which citizens can euthanize themselves. An artist creates a strange liquid with transformative properties, everything submerged within becomes marble...<br /><br />The second half contains stories set in Paris, centering around a group of bohemian art students and their female conquests. Beautifully written but a strange juxaposition after the former horror tales.<br /><br />Worth reading for the first four stories if you're a fan of classic horror, but a mixed bag as a collection.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16993925980936124210" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1732906307" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1732906307" />
    <a title="Daniel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/365191-daniel"><img alt="Daniel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1309463474p2/365191.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1732906307?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daniel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daniel" href="/user/show/365191-daniel">Daniel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1732906307" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15743204921437892127">A short take:<br/><br/>I read this nearly a year ago, and yet, flipping through it now and perusing the odd paragraph, many of these stories, along with their eerie plots and weird doings, come back to me and remind me of the great satisfaction I experienced in these pages. I am fascinated by the fact that "King in Yellow" stands out as an odd entry among Chambers' large career of now-forgotten prose. Whatever compelled him to pen these stories, I am so glad that we can enjoy them, today.<br/><br/>Some favorites: "</span>
  <span id="freeText15743204921437892127" style="display:none">A short take:<br /><br />I read this nearly a year ago, and yet, flipping through it now and perusing the odd paragraph, many of these stories, along with their eerie plots and weird doings, come back to me and remind me of the great satisfaction I experienced in these pages. I am fascinated by the fact that "King in Yellow" stands out as an odd entry among Chambers' large career of now-forgotten prose. Whatever compelled him to pen these stories, I am so glad that we can enjoy them, today.<br /><br />Some favorites: "Repairer of Reputations"--perhaps the 'must-read' of this anthology--; "The Messenger", deliciously pulpy; and "Is the Ux Extinct", which is silly and a lot of fun, especially given how dismal and serious weird fiction can be.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15743204921437892127" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_855414206" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/855414206" />
    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1547058-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540307275p2/1547058.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/855414206?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica" href="/user/show/1547058-jessica">Jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1547058-jessica?shelf=kindle-reads">kindle-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1547058-jessica?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1547058-jessica?shelf=2014">2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer855414206" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3732431771009541913">The first few stories of the collection are riveting and eerie; I thoroughly enjoyed the madness, picking this up after hearing about the literary references in True Detective. The fun tapers off and becomes kind of tedious by the end of the book. There were some good surprises and fun, scary narrative. Enjoyed those parts.<br/><br/><br/>I'd give the first half of the book five stars and the second half two. So, three and a half stars total. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('pyeUTx5taZNnvqSNwznIweDDK+8WmigpfX/zm+JAYGUWJ28RxTHxuaAXq6mBkMdbUHdB44WsT+k7h4POIXi6JQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('GJqUB2aAHJycCnquKiVCLa0D6ADn4Onb24e7DhD6Ch6pmm9ZvdyEtlujdYpojE23HbeCDHTWjhudf8tb08LQXg==')})
  }
//]]>

O<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText6841377427241032191\" style=\"display:none\">The Great God Pan&quot; is a novella written by Arthur Machen. A version of the story was published in the magazine Whirlwind in 1890, and Machen revised and extended it for its book publication (together with another story, &quot;The Inmost Light&quot;) in 1894. On publication it was widely denounced by the press as degenerate and horrific because of its decadent style and sexual content, although it has since garnered a reputation as a classic of horror. Machen’s story was only one of many at the time to focus on Pan as a useful symbol for the power of nature and paganism. Perhaps no figure better embodies the transition from the Gothic tradition to modern horror than Arthur Machen. In the final decade of the nineteenth century, the Welsh writer produced a seminal body of tales of occult horror, spiritual and physical corruption, and malignant survivals from the primeval past which horrified and scandalized late-Victorian readers. Machen\'s &quot;weird fiction&quot; has influenced generations of storytellers, from H. P. Lovecraft to Guillermo Del Toro - and it remains no less unsettling today. This new collection, which includes the complete novel The Three Impostors as well as such celebrated tales as The Great God Pan and The White People, constitutes the most comprehensive critical edition of Machen yet to appear. In addition to the core late-Victorian horror classics, a selection of lesser-known prose poems and later tales helps to present a fuller picture of the development of Machen\'s weird vision.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/57739.Robert_W_Chambers">About Robert W. Chambers</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/57739.Robert_W_Chambers"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1207157697p3/57739.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/57739.Robert_W_Chambers">Robert W. Chambers
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8254747081465588260">Robert William Chambers was an American artist and writer.<br/><br/>Chambers was first educated at the Brooklyn Polytechnic Institute,and then entered the Art Students' League at around the age of twenty, where the artist Charles Dana Gibson was his fellow student. Chambers studied at the École des Beaux-Arts, and at Académie Julian, in Paris from 1886 to 1893, and his work was displayed at the Salon as ear</span>
  <span id="freeText8254747081465588260" style="display:none">Robert William Chambers was an American artist and writer.<br /><br />Chambers was first educated at the Brooklyn Polytechnic Institute,and then entered the Art Students' League at around the age of twenty, where the artist Charles Dana Gibson was his fellow student. Chambers studied at the École des Beaux-Arts, and at Académie Julian, in Paris from 1886 to 1893, and his work was displayed at the Salon as early as 1889. On his return to New York, he succeeded in selling his illustrations to Life, Truth, and Vogue magazines. Then, for reasons unclear, he devoted his time to writing, producing his first novel, In the Quarter (written in 1887 in Munich). His most famous, and perhaps most meritorious, effort is <i>The King in Yellow</i>, a collection of weird short stories, connected by the theme of the fictitious drama <i>The King in Yellow</i>, which drives those who read it insane.<br /><br />Chambers returned to the weird genre in his later short story collections <i>The Maker of Moons</i> and <i>The Tree of Heaven</i>, but neither earned him such success as <i>The King in Yellow</i>.<br /><br />Chambers later turned to writing romantic fiction to earn a living. According to some estimates, Chambers was one of the most successful literary careers of his period, his later novels selling well and a handful achieving best-seller status. Many of his works were also serialized in magazines.<br /><br />After 1924 he devoted himself solely to writing historical fiction.<br /><br />Chambers for several years made Broadalbin his summer home. Some of his novels touch upon colonial life in Broadalbin and Johnstown.<br /><br />On July 12, 1898, he married Elsa Vaughn Moller (1882-1939). They had a son, Robert Edward Stuart Chambers (later calling himself Robert Husted Chambers) who also gained some fame as an author.<br /><br />Chambers died at his home in the village of Broadalbin, New York, on December 16th 1933.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8254747081465588260" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/954927-the-king-in-yellow-and-other-horror-stories">Quotes from The King in Yello...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;This is the thing that troubles me, for I cannot forget Carcosa where black stars hang in the heavens; where the shadows of men's thoughts lengthen in the afternoon, when the twin suns sink into the lake of Hali; and my mind will bear for ever the memory of the Pallid Mask. I pray God will curse the writer, as the writer has cursed the world with its beautiful stupendous creation, terrible in its simplicity, irresistible in its truth--a world which now trembles before the King In Yellow.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/1074051-this-is-the-thing-that-troubles-me-for-i-cannot">39 likes</a>

          </div>
